  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_45461f23-095f-4613-9ab3-5b8c15d167ed'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11529925677197932511">Otherland. In many ways it is humankind's most stunning achievement: a private, multidimensional universe built over two generations by the greatest minds of the twenty-first century. But this most exclusive of places is also one of the world's best kept secrets, created and controlled by an organization made up of the world's most powerful and ruthless individuals, a priv</span>
  <span id="freeText11529925677197932511" style="display:none">Otherland. In many ways it is humankind's most stunning achievement: a private, multidimensional universe built over two generations by the greatest minds of the twenty-first century. But this most exclusive of places is also one of the world's best kept secrets, created and controlled by an organization made up of the world's most powerful and ruthless individuals, a private cartel known--to those who know of their existence at all--as The Grail Brotherhood. Though their purpose in creating Otherland is still a mystery, it may not remain so for long. For they have exacted a terrible price from humanity in the process, and even their highly organized global conspiracy cannot hide the nature of their crimes forever. And now a small band of adventurers has penetrated the veil of secrecy that prevents the uninitiated from entering Otherland. But having broken into the amazing worlds within worlds that make up this universe, they are trapped, unable to escape back to their own flesh-and-blood bodies in the real world. And as dangers and circumstances split their party into small, widely scattered groups, their only hope of reuniting lies in returning again and again to the River that flows--in one form or another--through all the worlds.<br /><br />But the odds seem to be completely against them as they--and the one outsider with whom they might join forces--become hopelessly lost in realms where an Ice Age tribe's fears can only be quenched in blood...where insects are as large and deadly as dinosaurs...where they are caught in the war between a man made of straw and one made of tin...where cartoon ads take on a life of their own...where humans strive to survive in the aftermath of an alien invasion...and where one among their party is actually The Grail Brotherhood's most terrifying weapon--a sociopathic killer who has never failed and whose current mission is to make certain that not even one member of this little invasion force lives long enough to reveal the truth about Otherland to the people of Earth...</span>
  <a data-text-id="11529925677197932511" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1075542867" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1075542867?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=arc-review">arc-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=books-i-own-to-read">books-i-own-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1075542867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6804040692570278441">This is now my second book, not counting novellas, by Tad Williams and while I finished it, I will in fact not be continuing on with the series. <br/><br/>Book 1 in the Otherland series was just interesting enough to continue and finally the ending ramps things up and I was actually entertained. I get that this series is one long book to the author, but it's so absolutely boring I need something to happen and I start to expect it to at least be at the end of the book. Spoiler alert: <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[the end</span></span>
  <span id="freeText6804040692570278441" style="display:none">This is now my second book, not counting novellas, by Tad Williams and while I finished it, I will in fact not be continuing on with the series. <br /><br />Book 1 in the Otherland series was just interesting enough to continue and finally the ending ramps things up and I was actually entertained. I get that this series is one long book to the author, but it's so absolutely boring I need something to happen and I start to expect it to at least be at the end of the book. Spoiler alert: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the ending was barely less boring <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Again, just about nothing happens. Yes we had some big-ish revelations but it was so not worth the tedium. <br /><br />Because, yet again, we have a hugely long book where absolutely nothing happens, or I should say, things happen, but they take so long to happen it's like nothing happens. Listening to A Game of Thrones right now really emphasizes this. Things are constantly happening in that book.<br /><br />To add to the tedium, the characters are suddenly going from one "land" within this computer system called "Otherland" to another with no end in sight. I just can't possibly see a reason for all this nothing.<br /><br />And if I haven't already warned enough about spoiling the ending, here's another warning, but the last book at least got my expectations up to believe I might get another solid, entertaining ending. And yet no. <br /><br />I have the entire series of Memory, Sorrow, and Thorn and this book really does not recommend it right now. And I do feel bad. I know there are lots of fans, Williams has had a huge impact on the fantasy genre and I definitely have seen glimmers of greatness, but by and large, there's just not enough going on to keep my interest anymore.<br /><br />2 out of 5 Stars (I finished it so that means something right?)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6804040692570278441" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19126246-kaitlin?shelf=my-sff-faves">my-sff-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1572336588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17732981994916509820">So, this one goes straight onto the favourites shelf becuase this continuation turned this series from one I really liked into one I loved. The story picks up straight after the ending of the previous book, and I really loved seeing the instant re-immersion.<br/><br/>Some of the elements of this series which I most enjoy: <br/>- The blend of Sci-Fi & Fantasy elements into a convincing, bizarre and fun world filled with exciting scenes.<br/>- The characters - there are SO MANY great characters within this series fro</span>
  <span id="freeText17732981994916509820" style="display:none">So, this one goes straight onto the favourites shelf becuase this continuation turned this series from one I really liked into one I loved. The story picks up straight after the ending of the previous book, and I really loved seeing the instant re-immersion.<br /><br />Some of the elements of this series which I most enjoy: <br />- The blend of Sci-Fi &amp; Fantasy elements into a convincing, bizarre and fun world filled with exciting scenes.<br />- The characters - there are SO MANY great characters within this series from Renie &amp; !Xabbu to Martine (who really developed a lot for me in this one with the addition of her diary entries and backstory) to Orlando and Fredricks (a gamer pair who are great friends) to Cristabel (a young girl and the narrative is told from her world-view so you see everything through a lens of innocence) to Paul (the lost wanderer) to all the others. We honestly get to meet so many fabulous characters and I loved all the plotlines which is marvellous becuase it's a long book.<br />- The pacing - I know for some people a slower story isn't what they like to see, but I find myself falling more and more in love with super chunky books and stories (if they are done well and spend the slow plot time to develop characters &amp; worlds)<br />- The imaginative worlds - This story is set in a world where VR (Virtual Reality) is a huge part of day to day life and some of the ultra high tech is so capable of simulation that it's virtually like you're in another world. We pass through all sorts of crazy places within this story. Some of my favourites being the Emlar land where all the Emilies live, the War of the Worlds version of London and the giant Kitchen world (you can see they're a bit crazy). We definitely see a lot of travelling in this book and see our character encountering all manner of creatures, cartoons and manifestations in these wacky worlds. <br />- The plot - we're following a group of characters who are trapped on the Net and travelling through various Sims. The plot didn't ever feel too drawn out for me (especially if you compare it to something like Malazan or Wheel of Time - both super long yet I enjoy both a lot) and I found myself speeding through the majority of the audiobook (which is excellent by the way) in a day when I was travelling. <br />- The diverse elements - we have characters from all walks of life and from all over the world. Although it's set in South Africa predominantly when we follow the characters of !Xabbu and Renie, we also have an Englishman, Frenchwoman, Australian people and much more. I also love that we have people from vastly different cultures even within the same country like !Xabbu who is from a Bushamen tribe and has excellent stories to tell about this. <br />- The fun - this story truly is that. I feel as though we're always encountering new things and it's always a little on the crazy side. We get to see God-like beings ruling over their own specially crafted domains, meet the three blind mice and the scarecrow from Oz, and a world where everyone has the same name. All of this, and much more, made this into a crazy story but one I always knew was filled with vibrant, imaginative ideas.<br /><br />Overall I really, really loved this. I whizzed through the book and I devoured it, and I NEED to go into the next book and final book really, really soon. I just found this to be a book which I loved from start to end, and I think it really worked out well for me at the time to be travelling and binge reading this. 5*s and I will certainly saw this is a series which stays on your mind and is just filled with life. Highly recommend this story!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17732981994916509820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer6049678327953544748">Filler.<br/><br/>The first novel was long, but it was unraveling a mystery. This is just the main characters being herded through sim after sim, with a few character in the real world having enough screen time to be reminded that they exist. It gets old, because it's not necessary to the plot.<br/><br/>1. A character (Paul Jonas) or team of them (Rennie, !Xabbu) land in a sim word reminding us of something, sometimes blatantly.<br/><br/>2. They get captured or chased.<br/><br/>3. They leave to the next.<br/><br/>This is the bulk of the book. Wh</span>
  <span id="freeText6049678327953544748" style="display:none">Filler.<br /><br />The first novel was long, but it was unraveling a mystery. This is just the main characters being herded through sim after sim, with a few character in the real world having enough screen time to be reminded that they exist. It gets old, because it's not necessary to the plot.<br /><br />1. A character (Paul Jonas) or team of them (Rennie, !Xabbu) land in a sim word reminding us of something, sometimes blatantly.<br /><br />2. They get captured or chased.<br /><br />3. They leave to the next.<br /><br />This is the bulk of the book. What's left is:<br /><br />4. Plot events that don't have any real resolution.<br /><br />5. Introducing even more characters, like a police detective hunting Dread, or a virtual actor.<br /><br />6. A very tiny amount of plot events that set up real difficulties.<br /><br />The problem with this is that there are three more books in the series. If this were setting up the last volume, it could be forgiven. But this is just a middle, filler novel, and is souring me on the series. It's still very well written, to the point where each sim could be its own novel. There are times when some great moments peek through. !Xabbu as always is a wonderful character, and each character is different enough not to blur together.<br /><br />Still, the sheer amount of running in place is frustrating, and the fact that this wont be neatly tied up in a third volume reduces the rating I give. These are not slender books at all.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14044459672918553318"><b>Executive Summary:</b> Slow start, and many slow places throughout. The good parts make up for a lot of it, but for that reason I'm rounding my 3.5 stars down.<br/><br/><b>Audio book:</b> Another great job by George Newbern. He definitely <br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>I really enjoyed the first book. Not so much for the characters, but for the setting and the cool ideas. I've always loved the idea of virtual worlds, and Mr. Williams made an excellent blend of Fantasy and Sci-Fi that seemed to hit my buttons in the right way.<br/><br/>Unfort</span>
  <span id="freeText14044459672918553318" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> Slow start, and many slow places throughout. The good parts make up for a lot of it, but for that reason I'm rounding my 3.5 stars down.<br /><br /><b>Audio book:</b> Another great job by George Newbern. He definitely <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />I really enjoyed the first book. Not so much for the characters, but for the setting and the cool ideas. I've always loved the idea of virtual worlds, and Mr. Williams made an excellent blend of Fantasy and Sci-Fi that seemed to hit my buttons in the right way.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the the cool ideas of the first one weren't enough to overcome some slowness, and the characters were more important to my enjoyment of the book. I found some of them annoying, or uninteresting, and it made their plotlines a bit slower. <br /><br />Renie who I enjoyed in the first book, got on my nerves at times. Thankfully !Xabbu was there to help that story along. The most interesting plotline for me was probably Orlando, though Paul's story was pretty good as too. The rest of them I found good at times, and very slow at times. It felt like there were far too many POVs this go around. I guess with a 4 book door stopper series like this, that's to be expected, but I feel some of it could have been tightened up.<br /><br />Much of this book seemed to be a way for Mr. Williams to live out fantasy of worlds he'd like to visit/explore from history and/or fiction. I suspect if he chose more worlds that I found fascinating, I'd have enjoyed those parts much more. I found the time spent in bug land particularly tedious.<br /><br />Yet somehow despite all this, I still enjoyed the book. The ideas and the overarching story have its hooks into me. I want to know what happens next. I will definitely be picking up the third book once my audio time frees up a little. I'm just hoping the pace of the story picks up in the next book.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_14147222" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14147222" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/858949-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1208350750p2/858949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/14147222?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/858949-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9781857237641" href="/book/show/10093.River_of_Blue_Fire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/858949-chris?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/858949-chris?shelf=top-shelf">top-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14147222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16699280601825846776">When last we left Our Heroes, they were caught in the Otherland - an immense virtual reality program built by people with more money than God - with no idea where to go and no idea what to do. They were lost, confused and had no way out.<br/><br/>Oh yes - back before Neo got his clock punched by Agent Smith, Renie, !Xabbu, Orlando, Fredericks and all the other Otherland explorers discover that they are in more danger than they realize - if they die on the network, then they'll die in real life. And, almos</span>
  <span id="freeText16699280601825846776" style="display:none">When last we left Our Heroes, they were caught in the Otherland - an immense virtual reality program built by people with more money than God - with no idea where to go and no idea what to do. They were lost, confused and had no way out.<br /><br />Oh yes - back before Neo got his clock punched by Agent Smith, Renie, !Xabbu, Orlando, Fredericks and all the other Otherland explorers discover that they are in more danger than they realize - if they die on the network, then they'll die in real life. And, almost right out of the gate, people start dying. Whether they're tiny biologists living among the ants or a lifetime gamer warring against the different factions of a twisted Oz, they die in unpleasant and, ultimately real ways. And it's up to our heroes to not only avoid death themselves, but also to figure out what the hell they're supposed to be doing in there.<br /><br />One of the things I like about this series is that Tad Williams openly admits to stealing - er, paying homage to the great writers of the past. At the end of book one, when all the main characters have been gathered together and are being told about the great dangers they will face, and how they are part of a plan to defeat the Grail Brotherhood and their Nefarious Scheme, most of the people there want nothing to do with it. It's up to Orlando Gardiner, our young barbarian warrior-slash-progeriac teenager to say, "Hey, this the the Council of Elrond! We have a mission here!"<br /><br />Unfortunately, while the Fellowship of the Ring gets a clear mission before leaving Rivendell, the Otherland explorers are scattered before they know what to do, and their main goal is to run for their lives. As this book progresses, they start to learn more about the vast Otherland network, what its nature is and why it was made. They also learn that it is unstable, and possibly a living thing in its own right.<br /><br />Almost immediately, the group gets split up. That is, as all ensemble writers know, the best way to really build a meaty story, and it works really well here. Unfortunately, while there are three groups, the strongest and most interesting characters get put into two of them. Orlando and Fredericks get sent off into a world more bizarre than any online gaming ever prepared them for; Renie and !Xabbu end up in a horribly twisted version of <i>The Wizard of OZ</i>, if Oz had invaded Kansas, taken over, and started a three-way fight between the Scarecrow, the Lion and the Tin Man.<br /><br />This leaves us with the third and largest group being somewhat less interesting than the others. Not completely, of course - we have a blind woman who can sense the information flow of the simulation, a teenage net-freak who only speaks in online slang, a campy death-clown named Sweet William, a Chinese grandmother and an abrasive German woman. They're not bad characters by any means, and each one is special in his or her own right. It's just that most of them were introduced later in the first book, and so we've had less time to get to know them. Putting a more familiar character in that group might have made them more interesting, or it might have overshadowed them. Who knows?<br /><br />One thing that the third group has, however, is a secret - one of them is not who he or she appears to be. One of them has been co-opted by the sociopathic assassin, Dread. The only one with the freedom to go on and offline at will, he has nearly godlike power at his fingertips. And he intends to use it.<br /><br />I can imagine that Tad Williams had a great deal of fun working out these novels, mainly because he created a concept that allowed for incredible freedom in world-building. After all, on a super-powerful VR platform, any conceivable simulation can be created. So whether it is the mythical land of Xanadu, a cartoon kitchen where the groceries come to life at night, a world where people fly like birds, or the legendary land of Ithaca, the settings in these books are only limited to what Williams can think up and work with. <br /><br />What's really interesting is that he seems to take great pleasure in reminding us that we are, in fact, reading a story - he goes so far as to have one character reflect on exactly what <i>kind</i> of character he is. People are reminding themselves that they're not in a story, even though they are, and at the same time recognizing that the entire structure of their virtual universe is patterned on the rules of fiction. It's a strange type of meta-fiction that rewards the careful reader.<br /><br />So, as the book comes to a close, we have some new threads to follow. The Otherland explorers begin to find their purpose and learn about their situation. We've met a strange type of character which exists in many worlds at once - the beautiful, birdlike woman who tries to help Paul Jonas and Orlando Gardiner find their way; the horrible Twins, whose only job is to pursue Paul Jonas wherever he may go. These people can be found around any corner, and the outcome of meeting them is always uncertain.<br /><br />Offline, real-world investigations into the mysterious comas that afflict children begin to bear fruit - a young lawyer named Catur Ramsey is trying to help the parents of Orlando and Fredericks find out what happened to their children, and the search leads him to a strange woman, Olga Pirofski, who may have a vital clue. Renie's father involves himself with some very dangerous people indeed. The police in Sydney find themselves working on a five year-old murder case that will eventually lead them to the malicious assassin/hacker Dread. A mysterious group called The Circle makes itself known to a select few, and reveals its mission - to oppose the Lords of the Otherland and their relentless pursuit of immortality. All through this, those Lords of the Otherland struggle amongst themselves to see who will ultimately control it.<br /><br />The tale becomes stranger with the telling, but I can guarantee - you'll be good and ready to jump right into book three....</span>
  <a data-text-id="16699280601825846776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4698211933726930678">8/10<br/><br/>In the second book of the series Tad Williams continues to impress as he has added more characters than the previous book, more worlds and much more incredible ideas combining them all into a complex, and weirder, story where only himself could have made.<br/><br/>The story continues right where the previous one left of with Williams expanding his world-building, making it even greater than what he showed in the first book, and with the protagonists going through incredible, and unbelievable, adventur</span>
  <span id="freeText4698211933726930678" style="display:none">8/10<br /><br />In the second book of the series Tad Williams continues to impress as he has added more characters than the previous book, more worlds and much more incredible ideas combining them all into a complex, and weirder, story where only himself could have made.<br /><br />The story continues right where the previous one left of with Williams expanding his world-building, making it even greater than what he showed in the first book, and with the protagonists going through incredible, and unbelievable, adventures while in the meantime some revelations start coming about the plans of their enemies and what they’re, ultimately, after.<br /><br />Of course the book has also some problems, though small, as I felt that the story drags a bit more than it needed (mostly in the middle of the book), but as it goes on it becomes more and more better and with the ending having a really good cliffhanger while Williams leaves a lot of promises for the next books.<br /><br />Overall I can say that, besides its few flaws, I’m quite pleased of how this book turned out in the end, as also with Williams' writing that I’m starting to believe that he actually fits better with Sci-Fi stories.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11384145972262484549">I think I'll try to write a review for every book I read from now on. I know not many read this probably, but it's good to put my thoughts somewhere. I will also keep every review as spoiler free as possible, so don't worry about anything major being said here. With all this said: here is my first daily review, Otherland: River of Blue Fire<br/><br/>PROS: Similar to the first book, Otherland has managed to make me use my imagination is ways that I never have before. The idea of the Net has allowed William</span>
  <span id="freeText11384145972262484549" style="display:none">I think I'll try to write a review for every book I read from now on. I know not many read this probably, but it's good to put my thoughts somewhere. I will also keep every review as spoiler free as possible, so don't worry about anything major being said here. With all this said: here is my first daily review, Otherland: River of Blue Fire<br /><br />PROS: Similar to the first book, Otherland has managed to make me use my imagination is ways that I never have before. The idea of the Net has allowed Williams to create a sort of surreal environment. <br /><br />The stakes are higher in the this book, there's more action, and the story <br /><br />CONS: So far, I've been pretty disappointed with the antagonists. For two whole books, all we've really gotten is the same old "rich and powerful want to take over the world" kinda of scenario. And quite frankly, I'm getting a bit tired of this. Sure, we have a couple people who we're supposed to hate like Dread, and maybe Osiris. It also seems like Nemesis is going to play a big role. Still, I haven't developed the level of "hate" yet for these people that I normally feel for your typical villains. Hopefully in the next two novels we'll get something deeper than "rich and power are bad."<br /><br />Another problem I have with this novel is the lack of story progression. I loved tumbling through the various simluations with the characters. While this was all fun, I felt it didn't exactly end up anywhere. <br /><br /><br /><br />Overall: 4/5</span>

<div id="review_632322282" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/632322282" />
    <a title="Patricia Hamill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12951093-patricia-hamill"><img alt="Patricia Hamill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452459538p2/12951093.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/632322282?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patricia Hamill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patricia Hamill" href="/user/show/12951093-patricia-hamill">Patricia Hamill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12964345-river-of-blue-fire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12951093-patricia-hamill?shelf=reviewed-by-me">reviewed-by-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12951093-patricia-hamill?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12951093-patricia-hamill?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer632322282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18299581886012856148">Enjoyable, but takes its time...<br/><br/>The second installment of the Otherland series by Tad Williams picks up where the last leaves off. The "heroes" gathered by Mr. Sellers at the Golden City narrowly escape into another simulation, one that seems perfectly normal except that they are now 1/100th their real size. Gigantic insects and birds populate the world, going about their natural activities, but those are hazardous when you're the size of the next meal. <br/><br/>Soon, events beyond their control shatter </span>
  <span id="freeText18299581886012856148" style="display:none">Enjoyable, but takes its time...<br /><br />The second installment of the Otherland series by Tad Williams picks up where the last leaves off. The "heroes" gathered by Mr. Sellers at the Golden City narrowly escape into another simulation, one that seems perfectly normal except that they are now 1/100th their real size. Gigantic insects and birds populate the world, going about their natural activities, but those are hazardous when you're the size of the next meal. <br /><br />Soon, events beyond their control shatter the small company and each remnant must find its own way through the increasingly disturbing simulations. Renie and !Xabbu find themselves in Oz gone wrong where they meet a mysterious man who can overcome the rules of the simulation and a naive young girl named Emily who needs rescuing. <br /><br />Meanwhile, Orlando and Fredericks find themselves in the kitchen sink of a cartoon simulation. Soon, they are drawn into a quest to save a baby match (yes, a match) called Little Spark from evildoers who have kidnapped him for nefarious reasons. The river becomes a stream of spilled water where Orlando, Fredericks and Chief Strike Anywhere's (the match's father) lives are threatened by ravenous salad tongs that call the river home.<br /><br />Shortly after Orlando and Fredericks are swept away, the others find themselves in a world where the river takes on the form of a jet stream, where flight is as natural as walking. Martine becomes the voice of this segment of the group, keeping a log of what's happening and to whom. The mystery of "who is Dread" takes hold as several of her log entries note anomalous behavior by various members, a mystery that keeps you guessing until the very end.<br /><br />Finally, Paul Jonas continues his quest for the mysterious winged woman who haunts his dreams. Plagued by the tireless Twins, once known as Finch and Mullet, he runs from simulation to simulation, some quite horrifying. Gally, a kid who is neither puppet (part of the program) or citizen (human guest) makes another appearance but fails to recognize Paul from before.<br /><br />In the "real world", the family and friends of those trapped play out their own dramas. Jeremiah is dismayed with Long Joseph abandons him to see his son who is still in the hospital. Christabel worries for her friend, Mr. Sellers, who has taken Cho-Cho, a scary street boy as his assistant. Catur Ramsey, a lawyer representing the Gardinar and Fredericks families, tracks down leads, including the skittish agent, Beezle Bug, who seems to want to help but cannot do so without his comatose master's permission, and one of the stars of a popular kids show on the net. And in Australia, a detective takes a closed case as a personal challenge and begins to unravel a mystery that may reveal the earliest conquest of a serial killer.<br /><br />A common theme throughout is the feeling of hopelessness, despair, and perhaps even boredom of both those trapped in Otherland and those in the real world. It's difficult at times to believe that things will get better.<br /><br />The River of Blue Fire is complex, vivid, and at times scary. The action is intense and hard to predict, which is something I like in a story, and the characters are well-developed and interesting. <br /><br />On the other hand, this book reminds me of The Two Towers, by J.R.R. Tolkien, in that it's a continuation of a story in progress, sort of like a bridge. There is no true beginning or ending, though certain plot elements are resolved along the way. Like Tolkien, the story isn't rushed and in some places seems to linger just a bit too long. The length of the book and the pace may be daunting to those who are unprepared for it. If you have trouble finishing The Lord of the Rings or Battlefield Earth, you might have trouble finishing The Otherland series.<br /><br />Overall, however, I really liked this story. I would recommend it to anyone who likes epic fantasy, epic sci fi, or the idea of living in a fantastic, yet unpredictable, virtual world. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18299581886012856148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_178618464" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178618464" />
    <a title="Jacrify" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5344069-jacrify"><img alt="Jacrify" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178618464?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2011</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer3166560913131660701">I had a difficult getting into the first book of this series because of the incredible amount of detail and world building. I was also disappointed by the number of questions left unanswered. Well, the second book reaps the rewards of all the hard work in the first. This book flew by, and while it didn't answer all the questions put forth by the first (and raised several more), it answered enough to keep me interested.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1121653116" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1121653116" />
    <a title="terpkristin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3392444-terpkristin"><img alt="terpkristin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438465987p2/3392444.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1121653116?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="terpkristin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="terpkristin" href="/user/show/3392444-terpkristin">terpkristin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3392444-terpkristin?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3392444-terpkristin?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3392444-terpkristin?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3392444-terpkristin?shelf=sffaudio">sffaudio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3392444-terpkristin?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1121653116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5720277872376516116">Audiobook from Penguin Audio<br/>Narrated by George Newbern<br/>Length: 24.5 hours<br/><br/>The sequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/212211107' rel='nofollow noopener'>City of Golden Shadow</a> and the 2nd book (of 4) in the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/43762-otherland' rel='nofollow noopener'>Otherland</a> series, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10084.River_of_Blue_Fire__Otherland___2_' title='River of Blue Fire (Otherland, #2) by Tad Williams' rel='nofollow noopener'>River of Blue Fire</a> is a solid "middle book" in the series.<br/><br/>Picking up where <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28695.City_of_Golden_Shadow__Otherland___1_' title='City of Golden Shadow (Otherland, #1) by Tad Williams' rel='nofollow noopener'>City of Golden Shadow</a> left off, this book moved the pieces of all the players in the story without seeming to progress the plot too much. This is a common feature of "middle books" so was expected, though made the reading (listening) slow sometimes. At the point that </span>
  <span id="freeText5720277872376516116" style="display:none">Audiobook from Penguin Audio<br />Narrated by George Newbern<br />Length: 24.5 hours<br /><br />The sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/212211107" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Golden Shadow</a> and the 2nd book (of 4) in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43762-otherland" rel="nofollow noopener">Otherland</a> series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10084.River_of_Blue_Fire__Otherland___2_" title="River of Blue Fire (Otherland, #2) by Tad Williams" rel="nofollow noopener">River of Blue Fire</a> is a solid "middle book" in the series.<br /><br />Picking up where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28695.City_of_Golden_Shadow__Otherland___1_" title="City of Golden Shadow (Otherland, #1) by Tad Williams" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Golden Shadow</a> left off, this book moved the pieces of all the players in the story without seeming to progress the plot too much. This is a common feature of "middle books" so was expected, though made the reading (listening) slow sometimes. At the point that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28695.City_of_Golden_Shadow__Otherland___1_" title="City of Golden Shadow (Otherland, #1) by Tad Williams" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Golden Shadow</a> left off, the "hero" group was somewhat divided, with Renie and Xabbu in one simulation, Orlando and Fredericks in another, and the rest of the "hero" group in yet another sim. Paul Jonas' sim, too, went through a few worlds, separated from the rest of the crew. Much of this book was spent with them still spilt, each learning more about the rules of the simulation world through their experiences in the world. Martine's character, and her disability, were explored in detail in this book, bringing her to the forefront of the third hero group as a main character (to go along with Renie and Orlando). The bad guys also moved, and some of their motives were identified...and the mysterious Sellers, while staying in one (hidden) location, seemed to be doing more to try to help bring down the Otherland.<br /><br />All in all, there isn't much to say about this book that I didn't say about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28695.City_of_Golden_Shadow__Otherland___1_" title="City of Golden Shadow (Otherland, #1) by Tad Williams" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Golden Shadow</a>. I enjoyed this book, though didn't think it was as strong as the first book in the series. In this book, author Tad Williams had some fun with the simulation worlds, making alternate worlds of popular stories such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8909.The_War_of_the_Worlds" title="The War of the Worlds by H.G. Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">The War of the Worlds</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/236093.The_Wonderful_Wizard_of_Oz__Oz___1_" title="The Wonderful Wizard of Oz (Oz, #1) by L. Frank Baum" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wonderful Wizard of Oz</a>. It was fun to go through the book and try to see what book was referenced (if any) for each sim world. The book was fun and the cyberpunk ideas were interesting, but there was nothing new introduced in this book. The rules were better defined through the course of the plot, but there wasn't a lot of actual progression towards the heroes saving the day (or not). <br /><br />The audiobook was great to listen to, if the narration was slightly slow. I listened to it slightly sped up (using the 1.5x feature for spoken word playback on my iPhone) and it seemed perfect. The only downside to listening to these books in audio is that now I want the 3rd book in the series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10090.Mountain_of_Black_Glass__Otherland___3_" title="Mountain of Black Glass (Otherland, #3) by Tad Williams" rel="nofollow noopener">Mountain of Black Glass</a> to come out in audio...I'm not sure when or if it will be done, but I hope that it does come soon so that I can continue listening instead of having to switch to some printed media. Audiobooks are a great way to experience this series (so far).</span>
  <a data-text-id="5720277872376516116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_86799087" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/86799087" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1542839-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1228753802p2/1542839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/86799087?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/1542839-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1542839-mike?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer86799087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7461276316607604179">The second book in the Otherland series again makes clear that Tad Williams is in no hurry. He will spin his tale out in his good time, so if you are heading for the beach for a week, I recommend this series. Williams does many surprising things in this novel, which keeps it interesting. For one thing, he adds to his already immense cast of characters and story lines, pulling in peripheral characters and developing them in a workman-like way, adding perspectives and really having fun with the wo</span>
  <span id="freeText7461276316607604179" style="display:none">The second book in the Otherland series again makes clear that Tad Williams is in no hurry. He will spin his tale out in his good time, so if you are heading for the beach for a week, I recommend this series. Williams does many surprising things in this novel, which keeps it interesting. For one thing, he adds to his already immense cast of characters and story lines, pulling in peripheral characters and developing them in a workman-like way, adding perspectives and really having fun with the world he has created. Secondly, he takes a group of characters, four of which you are invested in and five you essentially know nothing about. Traditionally, you'd think the other five would be used to reflect back on the characters we know. Instead, Williams splits them up exactly along those lines, leaving five ciphers together, and creates a murder mystery with them. It seemed as if he were going to spin out this mystery across the remaining three books - but he resolves it in this one. Challenging stale narrative forms in the way he is doing here requires a pretty deft touch, and Williams handles it nicely. <br /><br />The characters are again more a means to showcase the worlds he imagines - in this world where nearly anything imaginable is possible. Quite a nice read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7461276316607604179" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2030897415" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2030897415" />
    <a title="JazzRJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7308482-jazzrj"><img alt="JazzRJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490244037p2/7308482.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2030897415?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JazzRJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JazzRJ" href="/user/show/7308482-jazzrj">JazzRJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2030897415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8052219151182360385">This book was a tough one to settle on a star rating for me. I will admit that in the beginning there where some elements of it that I enjoyed more than others. However, as the story continued it came together in a really wonderful way. Which made me feel silly for not enjoying some of the earlier bits as much. Plus, all of the book was a very cool wild ride, and I found myself really enjoying listening to the audiobook of this book while reading along in my physical copy. The audio book of is p</span>
  <span id="freeText8052219151182360385" style="display:none">This book was a tough one to settle on a star rating for me. I will admit that in the beginning there where some elements of it that I enjoyed more than others. However, as the story continued it came together in a really wonderful way. Which made me feel silly for not enjoying some of the earlier bits as much. Plus, all of the book was a very cool wild ride, and I found myself really enjoying listening to the audiobook of this book while reading along in my physical copy. The audio book of is pretty great. In the end I realized that this 2nd book in the series was great too. I just needed to trust the story. So even though I would say my overall rating of this first reading of River of Blue Fire would be something like a 4.75 stars I'm going to round up to 5 because I think if/when I reread it again I would give it 5 stars. Definitely going to continue on with the series because I must know how the story turns out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8052219151182360385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2642499263" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2642499263" />
    <a title="Steve R" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51602729-steve-r"><img alt="Steve R" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550608435p2/51602729.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2642499263?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve R" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve R" href="/user/show/51602729-steve-r">Steve R</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2642499263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14003415221695633160">Having reread this novel, I am impressed by how one can take it as a representation of several different genres. The difficulty in deciding which one it is to the greatest degree is somewhat of a drawback. Firstly, it is a cautionary tale of the potential dangers of technological developments. Then, it is a mystery novel. Then, it is a love story. Then, it is a moral homily. Finally, and I believe most frequently, it is an action adventure.<br/><br/>The conception of the Grail Brotherhood's 'immortality m</span>
  <span id="freeText14003415221695633160" style="display:none">Having reread this novel, I am impressed by how one can take it as a representation of several different genres. The difficulty in deciding which one it is to the greatest degree is somewhat of a drawback. Firstly, it is a cautionary tale of the potential dangers of technological developments. Then, it is a mystery novel. Then, it is a love story. Then, it is a moral homily. Finally, and I believe most frequently, it is an action adventure.<br /><br />The conception of the Grail Brotherhood's 'immortality machines' as they are aptly termed by Orlando, through which they attempt to establish VR simulations within which to live as Gods for all eternity, is truly an impressive one. The many manifestations these simulations take - an insect world, the England of the post-Martian attack from Wells' <i>War of the Worlds</i>, an Egyptian desert, the strange, strange kitchen, a prehistoric Neanderthal/Ice age world, Coleridge's Xanadu, Venice of the Renaissance, even the final colorless, featureless simulation <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[in which most of the members of Renie's infiltrating group find themselves <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>- are highly detailed and interesting conceptions. However, the underlying issue remains as to whether or not they are actually serving any legitimate purpose. Are they simply expensive playthings with no redeeming value and, in addition, with an insidious effect on those trapped in them? Is this really what we want from our computers and their associated technological possibilities: a complete escape from reality?<br /><br />Williams delights in keeping his readers guessing. His clues are suitably cryptic (seek the home of the wanderer and release the weaver, go to the black mountain, follow the darkness), and very rarely lead to anything tangible in less than at least a hundred pages. Yet even more so, the overwhelming issue of what has caused the children like Stephen, Renie's brother, to fall into seemingly irreversible comas, hovers over all the actions of both the good guys and the bad guys throughout the book spoiler&gt;with no real resolution reached. The purpose and progress of the Nemesis program is presented, but raises many more questions than it provides answers. The identity and motive of 'The Other', as well as his 'name that tune' query are puzzling, as is the makeup and background of 'The Circle' who supposedly oppose the Brotherhood. Why Paul continually meets the mysterious 'bird lady' is another issue to ponder, and the actual 'life' situation of Emily 22813 and Gally is unclear: they are supposedly not 'puppets', but does this mean they have real people personas in RL? Finally, the identity of the mole within the group is a frustrating issue, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[one that when it was resolved I had to realize that I'd been completely fooled! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The developing relationship Between Renie and !Xabbu is realized, at least on the part of the former, to resemble love. Still, what the exact form this emotion means to her is as yet undecided. Certainly, her feelings for Stephen, Paul's for Gally, Jeremiah's for the memory of Susan, Quan Li's for her granddaughter and even Long Joseph's for his son (though you could argue that his love for wine is really more pronounced) all betoken Williams' recognition that this interpersonal feeling is a strong contradiction to the selfish insensitivity of the Brotherhood to all human life except their own.<br /><br />The character of !Xabbu, bizarrely yet imaginatively represented throughout the majority of the novel in the simulated body of a baboon, once again provides the moral focus of the story: his stories, epigrams, dances, and general ruminative persona all make for a higher plane of consciousness that helps all those of his party to see through the confusion of their ever changing and challenging situations to what is most important: in the last novel, it was 'to hear the sun'; in this work, it is 'to see with one's heart'. Further, he states that has had 'to see again with the eyes that were given to me, to see with the heart of my people, something I have not done since we have been in this place, in this mirage.' <br /><br />Felix Jongleur's nigh-on two hundred year old life is working to make such a vision unattainable. Dread's atavistic pleasure in the act of killing represents a truly repugnant antithesis to !Xabbu's fundamental humanity. The new characters of Olga Perfosky, Decatur Ramsay and Calliope Skouros are welcome additions to the ongoing story. Even Dread's minion Dulcie provides a different perspective. The engaging back story of Martine is also a welcome interlude.<br /><br />But characterization falls short of the eternal thrust of narrative tension in Williams' approach (just as technological exposition largely precludes moral analysis): the book is almost a non-ending series of daring-do exploits and highly taut dramatic moments of peril. The crashing dragonfly plane, the attack by the giant praying mantis, the discovery of Sellars' underground lair by ChoCho, Orlando and Fredericks defending themselves against vicious salad tongs (!), the attack by the pirates in their gravy boat on the icebox in the kitchen simulation, Christobel's meeting General Yacoubian at her father's offices, the many encounters of Paul with Finney and Mudd (aka Mullet and Finch and/or Undine Parker and her husband), the nefarious Scarecrow and Lion in the Emerald City simulation, the perilous darkness of The Place of the Lost in Aerodromia, and the fight for the lighter with Dread: these are all virtually cinematic treasures of description and action.<br /><br />It is this which makes this work a four- rather than a five-star rating for me. I would much have preferred less excitement and more thought. As well, William's pattern of flipping from character to character or group to group from chapter to chapter (and even sometimes within chapters) makes for a disconcerting sense of progress. Paul does something, then you flip to Christobel, then to Renie and !Xabbu, then to Dread, then to Martine and her group, then to Felix, then to Dulcie, then to Olga, then to Calliope, then to Ramsay, then back to Renie and !Xabbu, by which time you have to do quite a bit of recalibrating to remember when and where you last encountered this character or group. It's as if I was reading sixty short stories more than a a six hundred page novel.<br /><br />Nevertheless, it does deserve a solid four star rating, if only for the imaginative construction of such a complex web of mysteries, characters, actions and moral issues.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14003415221695633160" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2618928506" />
    <a title="Ben Mckenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6169363-ben-mckenna"><img alt="Ben Mckenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314749029p2/6169363.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2618928506?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ben Mckenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ben Mckenna" href="/user/show/6169363-ben-mckenna">Ben Mckenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2618928506" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18073919101508328382">I'm beginning to convince myself not to continue reading this series due to recognizing the sunk cost fallacy, because at this point I think I need to use logic. I didn't particularly like the first entry in the series because it was somewhat slow in plodding to its eventual end, getting everyone into Otherland.<br/><br/>Having finished the second volume, I am convinced I didn't know what plodding was last time. I could easily confine the salient plot points to 1/4 of the book, while considering the rest </span>
  <span id="freeText18073919101508328382" style="display:none">I'm beginning to convince myself not to continue reading this series due to recognizing the sunk cost fallacy, because at this point I think I need to use logic. I didn't particularly like the first entry in the series because it was somewhat slow in plodding to its eventual end, getting everyone into Otherland.<br /><br />Having finished the second volume, I am convinced I didn't know what plodding was last time. I could easily confine the salient plot points to 1/4 of the book, while considering the rest mostly filler.<br /><br />At this point, I would love to have read a tightly woven story following Renie, !Xabbu, Orlando, and Salome through a much more tightly constructed discovery of Otherland and how to deal with and learn the systems they encounter. Add in Paul's plot, and I think you'd have all the sprawling epic you need. Mr. Williams does much, much more than this in a way I think made the first two books much more yawn worthy. Suddenly you have Martine's group, Dreads group, and the continued saga of Cristabel and Mr. Sellars. You have some cops in Australia and a children cartoon actor.<br /><br />Its just aggravating because I know there is a shiny book in here, but its really kind of dulled once everything else is layered on top of the main threads.<br /><br />I'm sure in book 4 he weaves all these threads into a ton of pay offs, but the reviews for book 3 are making me want to give up. I can't do another book where 3/4 of the information is just world building and walking around, I want some plot to finally kick into gear and start moving forward.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18073919101508328382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_307119759" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/307119759" />
    <a title="Phil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2935621-phil"><img alt="Phil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1318005507p2/2935621.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/307119759?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phil" href="/user/show/2935621-phil">Phil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer307119759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2054233552476488528">These books take me forever to read in between the hustle and bustle of life. I often read lots of online material and currently working my way through the Sandman graphic novel so I have plenty of distractions to keep from completing a book if it isn't grabbing me. Although I can't say that I didn't enjoy following through with characters' journey through all the virtual worlds, it just didn't seem to grab me. There was never a moment where I simply couldn't put it down which means I was never </span>
  <span id="freeText2054233552476488528" style="display:none">These books take me forever to read in between the hustle and bustle of life. I often read lots of online material and currently working my way through the Sandman graphic novel so I have plenty of distractions to keep from completing a book if it isn't grabbing me. Although I can't say that I didn't enjoy following through with characters' journey through all the virtual worlds, it just didn't seem to grab me. There was never a moment where I simply couldn't put it down which means I was never rushing to read it. Hence why the three stars.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Tad Williams is great writer even if he is a little long winded which is probably why I haven't simply bailed from the series. I've pulled some great quotes I highlighted while going through the book and attached them to my status updates if your interested. Although Renie's dad is still a dolt, we really got to see Renie evolve from the more mild mannered lady of the first book. There's a few occasions where she snaps and shows a much harsher side. Although there has been some incredible experiences in these worlds and further insights into the characters, the plot is moving very slowly toward the group finally coming to grips with their surroundings and feeling a small glint of hope in possibly getting out of Otherland alive.<br /><br />Dread is a nasty piece of work. Can't wait to see the consequences of his 'endearing' needs catch up with him. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Anyway, I'm going to keep plodding my way through this series. Although the next book in the series is only about 650 pages or so, I noticed the last one is pushing on a 1000! It'll be the end the year before I get through these!<br /><br />I'm also finding that one of the great things about eBooks is having all the annotations and highlights digitized, but it did take me a while to figure out how extract all this information from both a Kobo and an iPad. Definitely not something they have made easy and the jury is still out whether it is worth the effort. I need to streamline how I make that work. Can't wait for a decent app utility to automate the process. I'm also looking into using Sigil to append my annotations directly into an ePub book. Not something I would usually spend the time doing, but as instructor I'm thinking this could be a great addition for students annotating their textbooks or my notes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2054233552476488528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1282771497?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary" href="/user/show/23948922-gary">Gary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1282771497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9039961386055056712">The Good, the Bad, and the Ugly<br/><br/>The Good -<br/>if you read my review for book one in the series, you know that one major flaw in an otherwise excellent presentation, was excessive editing errors. This book fixes that problem, and is what you would expect of high caliber literature.<br/><br/>The Bad -<br/>5 stars; 4.8 stars; 4.3 stars - the rating continues to drop (modestly; it’s still a very good book)…<br/>Mr. Williams has a very fertile imagination, and it is exciting to see what he can think up. However, traveling th</span>
  <span id="freeText9039961386055056712" style="display:none">The Good, the Bad, and the Ugly<br /><br />The Good -<br />if you read my review for book one in the series, you know that one major flaw in an otherwise excellent presentation, was excessive editing errors. This book fixes that problem, and is what you would expect of high caliber literature.<br /><br />The Bad -<br />5 stars; 4.8 stars; 4.3 stars - the rating continues to drop (modestly; it’s still a very good book)…<br />Mr. Williams has a very fertile imagination, and it is exciting to see what he can think up. However, traveling the river solely as an exercise in imagination, frequenting simulations with NO correlation to plot advancement gets, well, let me quote the character Paul about a third of the way through the book:<br /><i>“His first thought, as he struggled toward the surface of yet another river, was; I could get tired of this very quickly.”</i><br /><br />The Ugly -<br />There is an Indian Reservation in close proximity to the town where I live. The Native American population is integrated into general society, and one of their pet peeves is the perpetuation of a stereotyped 1950’s Hollywood Western Indian. They are very proactive in promoting a realistic picture of their culture, both historic and current. Because of that I am sensitive to the way they are portrayed in the cartoon section of the river journey. What Mr. Williams did here was no different than using the “N” word if writing about Blacks. It made me very uncomfortable. He could have kept the cartoon format without degrading racial perception of a particular culture.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9039961386055056712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_154868128" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154868128" />
    <a title="Aleah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3398219-aleah"><img alt="Aleah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436270185p2/3398219.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154868128?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aleah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aleah" href="/user/show/3398219-aleah">Aleah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3398219-aleah?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154868128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15960077735871035653">Otherland, a massive virtual reality network, is composed of an unknown number of worlds. It's funded by a mysterious group of the wealthy and powerful who call themselves Grail Brotherhood; and, though nothing is clear, the primary purpose of the Brotherhood seems to be the maintenance of their own long lives... even at the expense of countless other. Across the globe children are going into medically inexplicable comas, including Renie Sulaweyo's little brother Stephen. Renie suspects that Ste</span>
  <span id="freeText15960077735871035653" style="display:none">Otherland, a massive virtual reality network, is composed of an unknown number of worlds. It's funded by a mysterious group of the wealthy and powerful who call themselves Grail Brotherhood; and, though nothing is clear, the primary purpose of the Brotherhood seems to be the maintenance of their own long lives... even at the expense of countless other. Across the globe children are going into medically inexplicable comas, including Renie Sulaweyo's little brother Stephen. Renie suspects that Stephen's strange illness is somehow connected to Otherland. Renie and her friend, a South African bushman named !Xabbu, sneak into the Otherland network in hopes of saving Stephen. Once in they find they are not alone in their search, nor is the Otherland network all that it appears to be.<br /><br />Tad Williams has created an elaborate virtual reality landscape in this, his second installment of the Otherland series. I'm enjoying these stories as a delightful mix of fantasy and science fiction, two of my favorite genres. Most of the story occurs on a virtual reality network, yet each of the "worlds" (or VR servers) are as whimsical and imaginative as any fantasy novel. <br /><br />Warning: This book is not for the easily distracted. At one point I counted as many as nine (yes, NINE) separate storylines. I enjoy an overly complex plot as much as the next sci-fi/fantasy nerd, but even I found myself unsettled by all the jumping around.<br /><br />Still, with that caveat, I'm really looking forward to book three.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15960077735871035653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
