  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1826442297" />
    <a title="JD" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1273097-jd"><img alt="JD" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462138190p2/1273097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1826442297?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JD" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JD" href="/user/show/1273097-jd">JD</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1273097-jd?shelf=sci-fi-and-fantasy">sci-fi-and-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1826442297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16733639533755131019">River of Blue Fire is another sci-fi/fantasy beast. Two books into the Otherland series and nearly 1,500 pages total. <br/><br/>The things I enjoyed about the first book are still fun in book 2, particularly the continuing intrigue of the Dread story line, and the fun of the VR worlds in the Otherland network. Williams presents us with I believe 11 new virtual worlds that the characters stumble through, seeking escape from the system, and answers to the mystery of the Otherland network and the Grail Broth</span>
  <span id="freeText16733639533755131019" style="display:none">River of Blue Fire is another sci-fi/fantasy beast. Two books into the Otherland series and nearly 1,500 pages total. <br /><br />The things I enjoyed about the first book are still fun in book 2, particularly the continuing intrigue of the Dread story line, and the fun of the VR worlds in the Otherland network. Williams presents us with I believe 11 new virtual worlds that the characters stumble through, seeking escape from the system, and answers to the mystery of the Otherland network and the Grail Brotherhood. There are so many clever ideas here that fully capture my imagination. It's easy to get swept up in the fun of these sim worlds.<br /><br />This book did drag a bit for me in spots, compared to book 1. I found the sections dealing with Olga, Ramsey, Christabel, and Mr. Sellers to be particularly tedious, though I know that those plot lines will build to something as Williams continues to weave his threads together. Also found myself wishing that the mystery woman puzzle would play out a little faster.<br /><br />Still, a good read, especially on the strength of all of that world building Williams does.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16733639533755131019" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9459836745556957676" style="display:none">Well, the journey continues for the several groups who are loose in the system. The story goes further and deeper into the characters - good and sinister.<br />I enjoyed the journey, but I did take heed of the author saying that the series is really one BIG book - but publishers wouldn't let him publish the story as such a big book - and we wouldn't be able to carry it around he said also.<br />We did find out more information and some questions were not answered - I guess that is what the third book is for.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2791329224" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2791329224" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72598206-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534808407p2/72598206.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2791329224?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/72598206-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2791329224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15246377786071103024">As with the first Otherland book, I liked this one but didn’t love it. The worlds are interesting, the characters diverse and multifaceted, and there is plenty of mystery to keep me guessing.<br/><br/>Unlike the first book, though, after I finished this book I have not gone straight on to the next one. In fact, I felt like I needed a break for a while. That’s because the whole thing feels like it’s getting a bit repetitive.<br/><br/>How many more worlds will these travellers visit before achieving their quest? And </span>
  <span id="freeText15246377786071103024" style="display:none">As with the first Otherland book, I liked this one but didn’t love it. The worlds are interesting, the characters diverse and multifaceted, and there is plenty of mystery to keep me guessing.<br /><br />Unlike the first book, though, after I finished this book I have not gone straight on to the next one. In fact, I felt like I needed a break for a while. That’s because the whole thing feels like it’s getting a bit repetitive.<br /><br />How many more worlds will these travellers visit before achieving their quest? And what is the point? Yes, they have no control over where they travel, and they are flying blind, but the author is in control. And it seems like he just wants to indulge himself by creating hundreds of these places for his characters to struggle through. In a normal fantasy world that would be okay, because the crossing would be geographically necessary and each hazard passed would get them closer to their end point. In this world, it all seems pointless. They meet random people, discover the inner workings of each new place and face a whole variety of dangers; unless they find out information, though, none of it matters. They could go to a thousand different places and be no closer to their destination. And that makes it harder to care about their journey. All we need to worry about is that they survive.<br /><br />Paul Jonas and his narrow escapes epitomizes this. How many more times will he come a hairsbreadth from being captured by the evil twins? It almost starts to lose its effect after the dozenth time. I say almost, because I’m still terrified of him falling into their hands and still root for him to escape them every time. It seems that his story may be moving into a new phase, though, so I’m looking forward to seeing where it takes him in the third book. Hopefully away from constant near misses with the twins.<br /><br />Renie is starting to irritate me with her short fuse and consistently angry demeanour. I miss Simon, the far more sympathetic protagonist of the Sorrow, Memory and Thorn trilogy. There’s no one in this series that’s really like him. That’s fine, of course, but I do wish there was one main character I found completely sympathetic, and that I could really root for. That would make up for all the unlikeable or annoying characters we have to put up with – Dread, Christabel and, most notably, Emily. I really hope there’s a good reason Emily is involved, considering all the other characters and, presumably, all the readers find her irritating.<br /><br />I’m also confused by how Dread and Dulcie are able to log on and off at will but seemingly every other person in Otherland has lost the ability to get out of the system. I trust that will be explained at some point, but I would’ve expected that to be addressed before now, considering how large a part it has played in their travelling companions’ experience.<br /><br />I’m still intrigued in the different mysteries Tad Williams has set up and am looking forward to finding out what happens – I’d better jump into book number three before I forget the clues we’ve been given so far, and before I forget all the multitude of different characters we have to keep track of. I appreciate the lack of predictability plot-wise, and don’t have much idea what to expect from the remaining two books in the series. I do hope there will be less aimless wandering, though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15246377786071103024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('z7R94neUPeS1PxsAiffJzlRn0nhH5F9Y33zpm7qCX2BlhULwc/5QIkO3PG488cL7hDVmEJaat6dcHw+NNzbznQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nmdyx4R3usyWr31vTQAjMg/4rW4p4CXx0mPwUYQNOJ40Vk3VgB3XCmAnWgH4BigH36oZBviezQ5RABZHCbmUYw==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6867600034781238829">Tad Williams is a California-based fantasy superstar. His genre-creating (and genre-busting) books have sold tens of millions worldwide, in twenty-five languages. His considerable output of epic fantasy and science fiction book-series, stories of all kinds, urban fantasy novels, comics, scripts, etc., have strongly influenced a generation of writers: the ‘Otherland’ epic relaunches June 2018 as an</span>
  <span id="freeText6867600034781238829" style="display:none">Tad Williams is a California-based fantasy superstar. His genre-creating (and genre-busting) books have sold tens of millions worldwide, in twenty-five languages. His considerable output of epic fantasy and science fiction book-series, stories of all kinds, urban fantasy novels, comics, scripts, etc., have strongly influenced a generation of writers: the ‘Otherland’ epic relaunches June 2018 as an MMO on steam.com. Tad is currently immersed in the creation of ‘The Last King of Osten Ard’, planned as a trilogy with two intermediary novels. He, his family and his animals live in the Santa Cruz mountains in a suitably strange and beautiful house. @tadwilliams @mrstad</span>
